<user_name>JoAnn SkyWatcher, EFT</user_name><Time>1617899570612< /Time>< Rating>

<Text>Alameda Natural Grocery is the hippest place to shop for groceries in Alameda. In fact, some peeps come from the "mainland" to shop there.

As I entered the store from their parking lot, on the left was a bulletin board with information about music and children. On the right, there was a bakery display case. I couldn't resist getting a large crispy breadstick with seeds, jalapeno and cheese. I also got some Â chocolate chip, molasses, and oatmeal cookies--they were so delicious I almost ate them all before getting back in my car.

They have a fresh fish and meat market where there is a butcher to make those special cuts of meat. Also, the animal products come from animals that are raised humanely. You can actually smell the fish before you buy (who wants to buy old stinky fish?) They have a wide variety of foods for vegans, and people on special diets, too. They steer away from chemically processed foods, including GMO. They have a beautiful selection of organic fruits and vegetables including the largest selection of fresh mushrooms I have seen in the East Bay.

They carry just about everything you would expect for a natural food store. Something that surprised me located above their large selection of chocolate bars was some really beautiful large woven baskets. You can see them in my photos.

I love coming to this store!<//Text>< pictures>

< review>
There's something promising, even inspiring, about walking the aisles of the Alameda Natural Grocery. Always an interesting selection of products, from the dark chocolates to the spices, from the fresh fruits and veggies to the canned alternatives. All the coffee beans.

There's something grounding about seeing the prices; I'm frequently stopped short midway through reaching for something by the vanity or convenience margin added. Fresh, organic, and even exotic items are available everywhere, at competitive prices, so the ANG needs to step up their game.

There's great possibility here, but without the prices to match. I'll keep returning, getting those things which just can't be found elsewhere in the area, but it'll take a lot to make ANG my first shopping stop.< /review>

< user_name>
Darien Ratima</user_name>
<date>1576847962229<//date>< Rating>
5</Rating>
< Text>
My daughter introduced us to Maya's. She and her friends come here a lot.  This was my first *real* introduction to Honduran food although I've tried a random PUPUSA somewhere once before.

We strolled in on a lazy Saturday afternoon around 3:00 and was surprised to find nearly all the tables full - party atmosphere, loud music and everyone tight around their tables enjoying their food.  ..."Wait, what time is it again?"

The bottled beer was ice cold - that was such a good start.
Thank you Maya for knowing that serving beer less than freezing cold is not an option!

Service was a bit sketchy, not much interaction beyond the order, the food delivery and the check. But it was one server for all of us, so let's give her a break.

FRIED CHICKEN (5/5) Who orders Fried Chicken at a Mexican/Honduran restaurant?  I guess I do now.  As I was scrolling through Yelp photos of this place, the pictures of the Fried Chicken were reeeaaaally calling my name.  You have a choice of leg or breast and we went for the breast.  It was humongous.  It comes with a red dipping sauce that was really perfect.  I had such a wonderful time tearing apart the chicken - especially the crispy skin - and dipping it in the sauce.  I will go back for that chicken, and that day might be tomorrow.  Loved the chicken.

HABANERO SAUCE (5/5)  Yes, I'm listing a condiment and rating it as a main dish.  You'll find this sauce in one of those lovely plastic squeeze containers on your table.  I L O V E D this authentically HOT sauce. It was everything - such a great compliment to the meal.  I will go back for this sauce and I think a lot of people are doing the same thing, given the fullness of the restaurant at 3:00 in the afternoon.  This sauce should get promoted to a soup!  :)

BALEADA (5/5) A baleada (BAH-lay-ah-dah) is a Honduran quesadilla.  Honduran street food apparently. There are many variations, but Maya's version had re-fried beans, some cheese and maybe a secret sauce of some kind.  It didn't look like much, but it was very tasty and hard to stop eating.

PUPUSA (4/5)  These happy little discs remind me of tamales - think of them as round tamales but without the wrapper.  These were good too.  Again, presentation wasn't much, but they delivered on taste for sure.

Maya's is an excellent find, no doubt.  Clearly there are many others that found it way before me, but hey, I'm only one person trying to get around to over a thousand bookmarked restaurants.  What really thrills me, is that Maya's is just up the street from our new house that we're moving into very soon.  Which means - I'll be here like every other day.  Such happy thoughts!

Try this place for sure - unpretentious and sort of rough around the edges, but the food is undeniably good.<//Text>

< text>
Maya's Cafe is one of my very favorite restaurants! I crave their coconut seafood soup. The broth is so flavorful with the sweet and savory coconut milk, an array of seafood and plantains. The seafood is a combination of shrimp, crab legs, fish filet, mussels in the shell. All topped with chopped cilantro, with a side of rice. This is one of their deliteful Honduran dishes. My daughter had the carnitas fajitas. The pork was so flavorful! The tortillas are house made both flour and corn. They would be delicious even on their own. My husband had the Caldo, de Rez, a very flavorful, hearty beef and vegetable soup with tender fall off the bone beef, veggies and yucca.
Hmmm, even the chips and salsa are tasty! The menu is quite large with many Honduran and Mexican specialties.
This is a small family run restaurant. Everything is made fresh to order.
The service is great and friendly. I am looking forward to many more visits!!< /text>
